Deterministic Preprocessing and Interpretable Fuzzy Banding for Cost-per-Student Reporting from Extracted Records
Abstract
Administrative extracts are often exchanged as spreadsheets and may be read as reports in their own right during budgeting, workload review, and governance discussions. When an exported workbook becomes the reference snapshot for such decisions, the transformation can be checked by recomputation against a clearly identified input.
A deterministic, rule-governed, file-based workflow is implemented in cad_processor.py. The script ingests a Casual Academic Database (CAD) export workbook and aggregates inclusive on-costs and student counts into subject-year and school-year totals, from which it derives cost-per-student ratios. It writes a processed workbook with four sheets: Processing Summary (run record and counters), Trend Analysis (school-year cost-per-student matrix), Report (wide subject-level table), and Fuzzy Bands (per-year anchors, membership weights, and band labels). The run record includes a SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes to support snapshot-matched recomputation [8].
For within-year interpretation, the workflow adds a simple fuzzy banding layer [17] that labels finite, positive school-year cost-per-student values as Low, Medium, or High. The per-year anchors are the minimum, median, and maximum of the finite, positive ratios. Membership weights are computed using left-shoulder, triangular, and right-shoulder functions, with deterministic tie-breaking in a fixed priority order (Medium, then Low, then High). These weights are treated as decision-support signals rather than probabilities.
A worked example provides a reproducible calculation of a band assignment from the reported anchors and ratios. Supplementary material includes a claim-to-evidence matrix, a reproducibility note, and a short glossary that links selected statements to code and workbook artefacts.

bm:introduction.1bm:introduction.1\EdefEscapeHex1 Introduction1 Introduction\hyper@anchorstartbm:introduction.1\hyper@anchorend
1 Introduction
Cost-per-student tables derived from administrative extracts can carry substantial weight in budgeting, resource allocation, and governance discussions. A common workflow begins with an export from an operational system and ends with a wide table circulated for decision-making. In such settings, inspection depends on being able to rerun the same transformation against the same snapshot. Derived tables can then be reconciled with the stated rules and logged counters.
A deterministic, rule-governed, file-based workflow transforms a Casual Academic Database (CAD) export workbook into a processed workbook designed to support checking by recomputation and comparison [12]. The emphasis on well-described artefacts aligns with the FAIR (Findability, Accessibility, Interoperability, and Reuse) principles for data stewardship and reuse [16]. With byte-identical inputs and a stable runtime environment, the transformation is intended to produce consistent outputs, enabling reruns to be checked against the produced tables and the logged counters. The workflow records a SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes to support snapshot matching [8].
The workflow aggregates inclusive on-costs and student counts to subject-year and school-year totals, then computes cost-per-student ratios from those totals. The processed workbook contains four sheets. Processing Summary records run metadata, the input hash, and observed counts for row-handling decisions. Trend Analysis presents a school-year cost-per-student matrix that supports comparison across schools and years. Report contains a wide subject-level table organised by year. Fuzzy Bands records per-year anchors and membership weights, and assigns a deterministic label (Low, Medium, or High) to each eligible school-year cost-per-student ratio alongside the underlying ratios and the anchors used to generate those labels.
For within-year interpretation that remains checkable from reported values, the workflow adds a small fuzzy banding layer [17]. For each year, anchors are computed from finite, positive school-year cost-per-student values as the minimum, median, and maximum. Low, Medium, and High memberships are computed using left-shoulder, triangular, and right-shoulder functions, with deterministic tie-breaking in a fixed priority order (Medium, then Low, then High). Membership weights are treated as decision-support signals rather than probabilities.
Two research questions structure the analysis. RQ1 asks how a deterministic, rule-governed pipeline can be specified and evidenced so that its behaviour can be checked directly from code and workbook artefacts. RQ2 asks how an interpretable fuzzy banding layer can summarise within-year relative position while keeping ratios and anchors available for checking by recomputation.
Key terms used throughout are defined in the next section. Supplementary material includes a claim-to-evidence matrix for selected statements, a reproducibility note, and a short glossary of technical terms with brief examples.
bm:operational.1bm:operational.1\EdefEscapeHex2 Operational terms and scope2 Operational terms and scope\hyper@anchorstartbm:operational.1\hyper@anchorend
2 Operational terms and scope
Records are taken from a CAD export workbook and treated as a spreadsheet snapshot of casual academic teaching costs and student counts. The export includes fields labelled School, Subject No., Subject, and Teaching Session. The workflow extracts a four-digit year token from Teaching Session and reads Incl Oncosts and Student Count. “Inclusive on-costs” is used in the ordinary institutional sense of employment-related on-costs included in the cost amount [14].
The following definitions reflect the implemented behaviour in the processing script and how it is represented in the output workbooks. They also state boundaries that limit later interpretation to what can be checked directly in the artefacts.
bm:operational-defs.2bm:operational-defs.2\EdefEscapeHex2.1 Operational definitions2.1 Operational definitions\hyper@anchorstartbm:operational-defs.2\hyper@anchorend
2.1 Operational definitions
Deterministic, rule-governed processing denotes a fixed sequence of steps with defined row-handling rules and deterministic tie-breaking where applicable. When the input snapshot changes (for example, when new months are added), the outputs change accordingly, but the same rules are applied consistently. Given identical input workbook bytes and the same runtime environment, the transformation is intended to produce the same aggregated tables, counters, and per-year anchors. Reproducible computational work benefits from recording inputs, code, and execution context [12]. Reproducibility and replicability expectations motivate recording what is needed to rerun and check results [7].
Auditability is treated as an inspection property. A run can be inspected by recomputation and comparison of the produced tables against a known input snapshot. The processed workbook records a SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes and summarises observed row-handling outcomes and group counts [8].
Inclusive on-costs and student count are aggregated measures drawn directly from the export. Missing cost values are treated as 0.0 and missing student counts as 0 for aggregation, and both are counted as missing. Negative student counts are dropped.
Cost-per-student is computed as Total_Oncosts divided by Total_Students when Total_Students is greater than 0. Two boundary cases are tracked separately: No activity, where both totals are 0 and the ratio is reported as 0.0, and Undefined (0 students), where Total_Oncosts is greater than 0 but Total_Students is 0 and the ratio is left blank.
Anchors are per-year reference points (minimum, median, maximum) computed from finite, positive school-year cost-per-student values. These anchors are used for both heat map scaling in the Trend Analysis sheet and for fuzzy membership calculations.
Fuzzy banding is an interpretability layer that assigns Low, Medium, and High labels within each year using triangular membership functions [17] anchored by the per-year minimum, median, and maximum. The term “triangular” refers to the piecewise-linear membership curves defined by three anchor points (minimum, median, maximum), rising to a peak at the median and falling to zero at the extremes. Membership weights are treated as decision-support signals for within-year interpretation. Ties are resolved deterministically (Medium, then Low, then High). A corresponding band score on a 0 to 1 scale is reported for convenience.
bm:scope.2bm:scope.2\EdefEscapeHex2.2 Scope and non-goals2.2 Scope and non-goals\hyper@anchorstartbm:scope.2\hyper@anchorend
2.2 Scope and non-goals
The workflow is file-based. It reads a single Excel workbook treated as the authoritative export snapshot and writes a processed workbook. In the reported runs, the script was executed in Microsoft Foundry (Azure Machine Learning), which provided the file system context for the input and output files.
During parsing and aggregation, the workflow applies a documented rule set and records counters for observed row conditions and handling decisions. The processed workbook records a SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes to support later recomputation and comparison [8].
The fuzzy banding component is descriptive. It summarises within-year relative position among finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratios while keeping the underlying numeric ratios visible in the output.
bm:artefacts.1bm:artefacts.1\EdefEscapeHex3 Artefacts and data representation3 Artefacts and data representation\hyper@anchorstartbm:artefacts.1\hyper@anchorend
3 Artefacts and data representation
The evidence artefacts support claim checking by recording links between inputs, processing, and outputs [1, 13, 12].
bm:artefacts-used.2bm:artefacts-used.2\EdefEscapeHex3.1 Evidence artefacts used3.1 Evidence artefacts used\hyper@anchorstartbm:artefacts-used.2\hyper@anchorend
3.1 Evidence artefacts used
The evidence artefacts comprise (i) an input workbook serving as the CAD export snapshot (CAD_Contract.xlsx), (ii) a processed workbook (Processed_CAD_Contract.xlsx), (iii) the processor script (cad_processor.py [5]), and (iv) run logs capturing counters and metadata (cad_processor_execution.log and cad_processor.log).
Run identifiers are recorded in the logs, while the Processing Summary sheet of the processed workbook records run metadata and counters. The logs include:
-
•
cad_processor_execution.log, which appends one tab-separated line per run with status, input file name, output file name, and the input workbook SHA-256 hash.
-
•
cad_processor.log, which records trace messages including the input workbook SHA-256 hash, the detected input table (sheet name and header row), and output write completion.
Both logs are plain text and can be inspected with standard editors.
The Processing Summary sheet in the output workbook records the SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes used in the logged run. Example values and labels in the narrative are de-identified and, where necessary, rounded or scaled to preserve the computation and inspection logic without exposing operational magnitudes.
Each row identifies a school and subject, indicates when the teaching occurred, and records the cost and student count that are later aggregated into per-subject and per-school summaries. Table 1 summarises the input column data dictionary used by the workflow.
bm:input-schema.2bm:input-schema.2\EdefEscapeHex3.2 Input table schema and data dictionary3.2 Input table schema and data dictionary\hyper@anchorstartbm:input-schema.2\hyper@anchorend
3.2 Input table schema and data dictionary
The workflow expects a header row that contains the required fields: School, Subject No., Subject, Teaching Session, Incl Oncosts, and Student Count. It maps these fields to worksheet positions. The year is derived from Teaching Session by extracting the first four-digit year token. Required names and accepted aliases are encoded in the processor rules, but the behaviour is defined by the header match and field mapping.
bm:table-location.2bm:table-location.2\EdefEscapeHex3.3 Table location and header detection3.3 Table location and header detection\hyper@anchorstartbm:table-location.2\hyper@anchorend
3.3 Table location and header detection
The workflow scans sheets in order and searches early rows to locate a header row that matches the required fields. It returns the detected sheet name, the header row index, and a mapping from logical fields to worksheet column indices. In the implementation, the scan range is bounded by fixed limits (30 rows, 60 columns), and alias handling normalises a defined set of header-name variants without manual edits to the input workbook.
In the example run, the Processing Summary records Input sheet = data and Header row (1-based) = 1. For the logged run, the required columns were found in the first row of that sheet. The processing log (cad_processor.log) records the same location using 0-based row indexing, while Processing Summary reports 1-based indexing.
bm:background.1bm:background.1\EdefEscapeHex4 Background and related work4 Background and related work\hyper@anchorstartbm:background.1\hyper@anchorend
4 Background and related work
Institutional reporting can serve academic leadership, professional services, and governance committees [9]. Espeland and Stevens describe commensuration as the social process through which quantitative measures are produced and interpreted in organisational settings [2]. When inputs are delivered as spreadsheets, the spreadsheet may be treated as the report itself, even where it primarily transports an authoritative export snapshot. In such settings, trust in derived tables depends on whether the transformation from snapshot to report is transparent, repeatable, and open to inspection [12, 16]. Where the input snapshot and the processor are available, the tables can be recomputed and compared. Where only the processed workbook is circulated, it remains readable and interpretable using standard spreadsheet functionality.
Provenance describes how outputs are produced from inputs so that results can be traced to specific transformation steps, supporting inspection and accountability in e-science workflows [1, 13]. SHA-256 is a standardised cryptographic hash function [8]. In this workflow, it is used as a content hash of the input workbook bytes, so that later runs can confirm whether the same snapshot was used for recomputation and comparison.
Fuzzy linguistic labelling provides a constrained interpretive aid by mapping numeric values to Low, Medium, and High while keeping the underlying ratios visible. A membership weight in indicates partial membership in a band and functions as a graded label rather than a probability [17]. Common membership functions, including triangular and shoulder forms, are used to keep the mapping transparent and parameterised [4, 11].
These concepts ground the deterministic preprocessing steps and the fuzzy banding logic used in the workflow.
bm:method5.1bm:method5.1\EdefEscapeHex5 Method: deterministic preprocessing and aggregation5 Method: deterministic preprocessing and aggregation\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5.1\hyper@anchorend
5 Method: deterministic preprocessing and aggregation
The workflow locates the extract table, normalises fields, streams rows, and aggregates to subject-year and school-year groups. It derives cost-per-student values when the student count is positive and records boundary cases when totals indicate no activity or an undefined ratio. Per-year anchors are computed from finite, positive school-year cost-per-student values. Where anchors are available, the workflow computes membership weights and assigns a band label. It writes a processed workbook with a fixed set of worksheets, including Processing Summary. The analysis focuses on the implemented transformation and the artefacts it produces.
The steps follow execution order and are linked to workbook outputs so that selection, cleaning, grouping, and summarising can be traced [10].
bm:method5-1.2bm:method5-1.2\EdefEscapeHex5.1 Overview of the pipeline stages5.1 Overview of the pipeline stages\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5-1.2\hyper@anchorend
5.1 Overview of the pipeline stages
For a single row in the input table, the process begins with header detection. It then trims and converts row values and assigns the row to subject-year and school-year groups. The detected sheet and header row are recorded in Processing Summary for inspection.
The pipeline stages implemented in the processor are table location, row streaming, aggregation, fuzzy band construction, and workbook writing. The output workbook uses fixed sheet names and order (Processing Summary, Trend Analysis, Report, Fuzzy Bands). Workbook properties are also fixed, including the creator string and preset created and modified timestamps. The pipeline uses a stream-based approach [15] in which rows are iterated from the worksheet and checked against the rule set as they are read. During streaming, the script increments counters for missing values, dropped rows, and other data-quality conditions. Given identical input workbook bytes and the same code version and rule set, the transformation is designed to be deterministic. Control flow depends on row content, the rule set, and the fixed ordering of operations [12, 7].
bm:method5-2.2bm:method5-2.2\EdefEscapeHex5.2 Pseudocode specification5.2 Pseudocode specification\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5-2.2\hyper@anchorend
5.2 Pseudocode specification
The listings make the rule set inspectable and support recomputation checks while keeping the summary prose focused on responsibilities. For a single row, the header position returned by locate_table() determines where streaming begins, stream_rows() yields rows beneath the detected header, and aggregate() decides whether the row is kept and assigns it to its group keys.
Listing 5.2 summarises header detection and table location in locate_table(). It establishes the input sheet and header row. These are recorded in Processing Summary.
Listing 1: Header detection and table location Input: workbook wb, scan_rows For each sheet ws in wb.worksheets in workbook order: For each row r from 1 to scan_rows: Read row values as strings Canonicalise each header cell (strip, map aliases) If all required logical columns are present: Return (sheet_name, header_row=r, col_map) If no sheet and row contains all required columns: Raise ValueError
Listing 5.2 summarises row streaming, row checks, and aggregation counters as implemented in stream_rows() and aggregate(). It defines the conditions under which rows are kept or dropped, how subject-year and school-year groups are formed, and the counters recorded in the Processing Summary.
Listing 2: Row streaming, row checks, and aggregation Input: input workbook, located_table loc Initialise counters in DataQuality dq Initialise subject_year and school_year aggregations For each worksheet row returned by stream_rows(input_path, loc): dq.total_rows_seen += 1 Extract fields by loc.col_index (School, Subject No., Subject, Teaching Session, Incl Oncosts, Student Count) If School or Subject matches summary-row pattern (Total|Sum|Result): dq.rows_dropped_summary_rows += 1 Continue If School, Subject No., or Subject missing or blank: dq.rows_dropped_missing_keys += 1 Continue Extract year from Teaching Session using regex If year missing: dq.rows_dropped_missing_year += 1 Continue Convert cost with to_float (missing treated as 0.0) If cost missing: dq.rows_with_missing_cost += 1 Convert students with to_int (missing treated as 0) If students missing: dq.rows_with_missing_students += 1 If students < 0: dq.rows_with_negative_students += 1 Continue Add cost and students to: subject_year[(school, subject_no, subject, year)] school_year[(school, year)] After streaming: For each group, compute cost-per-student and status with safe division: OK if students > 0 No activity if cost == 0 and students == 0 (ratio set to 0.0) Undefined (0 students) if cost > 0 and students == 0 (ratio left blank) Record group counts in dq and write output tables.
Listing 5.2 summarises output workbook writing, including the Processing Summary and derived sheets. It illustrates how the hash, counters, and fuzzy band outputs are recorded in the fixed workbook structure.
Listing 3: Workbook writing Compute input_hash = SHA-256(input workbook bytes) Create new workbook wb_out Write Processing Summary: hash, detected sheet and header row, counters, anchors Write Trend Analysis: school-by-year table of cost-per-student, per-year colour scales Write Report: per-subject report with per-year cost, students, and cost-per-student Build Fuzzy Bands: compute memberships for finite, positive school-year cost-per-student values Write Fuzzy Bands: per included school-year record with mu values, band label, band score, anchors Save wb_out to output filename
bm:method5-3.2bm:method5-3.2\EdefEscapeHex5.3 Row filtering and type conversion rules5.3 Row filtering and type conversion rules\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5-3.2\hyper@anchorend
5.3 Row filtering and type conversion rules
For a single row, this step checks whether the identifying fields are present and whether a year can be extracted from Teaching Session, then converts the cost and student-count values to numeric types. The rules define which rows are kept, which are dropped, and how missing values are handled for aggregation.
Rows are dropped if any identifying field is missing or blank, or if a four-digit year token in the range 1900 to 2099 is not detected in Teaching Session. Rows are also dropped if School or Subject equals (case-insensitive, after trimming) a summary marker such as “Total”, “Sum”, or “Result”, or if Student Count is negative. Corresponding counters are incremented. Missing or non-numeric Incl Oncosts values are treated as 0.0 for sums and counted, and missing or non-numeric Student Count values are treated as 0 for sums and counted. Cost-per-student is computed only when aggregated Student Count is greater than zero, and boundary cases are handled consistently with the workflow’s definitions of zero, missing, and undefined.
bm:method5-4.2bm:method5-4.2\EdefEscapeHex5.4 Deterministic means repeatable5.4 Deterministic means repeatable\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5-4.2\hyper@anchorend
5.4 Deterministic means repeatable
For a given run, the workflow’s outputs depend on the input workbook file bytes, the implemented rule set, and the runtime environment. If the input workbook changes between runs (for example, as monthly records are added), the outputs can change accordingly. In this setting, determinism supports interpretation: the workflow applies its rules in the same order for each run, so differences in outputs can be interpreted as reflecting differences in inputs and documented rule changes, rather than untracked processing decisions [7].
bm:method5-5.2bm:method5-5.2\EdefEscapeHex5.5 Audit-supporting Processing Summary5.5 Audit-supporting Processing Summary\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5-5.2\hyper@anchorend
5.5 Audit-supporting Processing Summary
The Processing Summary records the input workbook SHA-256 hash (computed over the saved workbook file bytes), the detected input sheet and header row, counters for row-handling and grouping, and year-specific anchor values used for heat map scaling and fuzzy banding when finite, positive values are available [8]. The hash provides a stable identifier for the input snapshot used for the run, the counters summarise key row-handling outcomes (including exclusions), and the anchors and rule-based outputs support recomputation of the banding for inspection.
Figure 1 shows the run entry point where the input workbook path is recorded, the input file SHA-256 hash is computed, and the processed workbook is written. The execution log line records a status token (OK), the input file name, the output file name, and the input SHA-256 hash for run identification.
The deterministic pipeline makes the consequences of the input snapshot checkable, including how many missing values were treated as zero and how many ratios were left undefined.
bm:method5-6.2bm:method5-6.2\EdefEscapeHex5.6 Zero vs missing vs undefined5.6 Zero vs missing vs undefined\hyper@anchorstartbm:method5-6.2\hyper@anchorend
5.6 Zero vs missing vs undefined
A zero value means that a numeric field is present and equals 0. A missing value means that the field is absent or non-numeric, is treated as 0 for aggregation, and increments a counter. The No activity case occurs when cost and student count , yielding a ratio of 0.0. The Undefined (0 students) case occurs when cost and student count , yielding an undefined ratio (cell left blank) to keep the boundary case visible.
The deterministic pipeline is followed by the fuzzy banding component, which operates on the computed ratios.
bm:method6.1bm:method6.1\EdefEscapeHex6 Method: interpretable fuzzy banding6 Method: interpretable fuzzy banding\hyper@anchorstartbm:method6.1\hyper@anchorend
6 Method: interpretable fuzzy banding
The workflow maps finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratios to Low, Medium, and High within each year using year-specific anchors and defined membership functions. The banding outputs are reported alongside the ratios as an interpretability layer that expresses the Low, Medium, and High labelling through membership weights [17]. The numeric ratios remain primary, and the workbook records the membership weights, the resulting band label, and the intermediate values used in the computation.
bm:method6-1.2bm:method6-1.2\EdefEscapeHex6.1 Anchor computation6.1 Anchor computation\hyper@anchorstartbm:method6-1.2\hyper@anchorend
6.1 Anchor computation
Anchors define the year-specific reference points used for heat map scaling and fuzzy banding. The script computes per-year anchors from the school-year table using the finite, positive cost-per-student values for that year (eligible values). Membership weights are computed only for years with at least one eligible value, using anchors derived from those values. Years without eligible values are recorded in Processing Summary as having no anchors. Using year-specific anchors keeps the banding comparable within each year rather than imposing a single scale across years. For each year, the anchors are defined as (minimum), (median), and (maximum) of the year’s eligible school-year cost-per-student ratios. The median is used as the central anchor because it provides a stable reference point under skew and outliers [6]. It is the middle value once the ratios are sorted. When the number of ratios is even, is the average of the two middle values, not the midpoint between the minimum and maximum and not the mean of all values. As an illustrative example, consider the four ratios (10.0, 12.0, 18.0, 30.0). The minimum and maximum are 10.0 and 30.0, and the median is the mean of the two middle values: . Numeric values in Sections 7.4–7.7 are synthetic examples used for illustration and do not correspond to an institutional dataset. The script records the anchors in the Processing Summary and repeats them alongside each school-year record in the Fuzzy Bands sheet. The next step uses these anchors to compute three membership weights on a 0 to 1 scale for each eligible value.
bm:method6-2.2bm:method6-2.2\EdefEscapeHex6.2 Membership functions6.2 Membership functions\hyper@anchorstartbm:method6-2.2\hyper@anchorend
6.2 Membership functions
Equations (1a)–(1c) define the membership functions used to compute Low, Medium, and High weights for each school-year record with a finite, positive cost-per-student value and defined anchors with . The weights lie on a 0 to 1 scale and indicate alignment with the within-year labels rather than probabilities. A numeric worked example illustrates the computation using the same anchors and equations.
The script writes these values into the Fuzzy Bands sheet as the Low, Medium, and High membership weights (Mu_Low, Mu_Medium, Mu_High) for each included school-year record. The implementation includes guards for degenerate anchor configurations to avoid division by zero. When anchors collapse, the Low and High shoulders reduce to step-like behaviour. The Medium function returns 1 only at and 0 otherwise, keeping membership weights well-defined.
bm:method6-3.2bm:method6-3.2\EdefEscapeHex6.3 Band assignment, scoring, and tie-breaking6.3 Band assignment, scoring, and tie-breaking\hyper@anchorstartbm:method6-3.2\hyper@anchorend
6.3 Band assignment, scoring, and tie-breaking
For each included school-year record with a finite, positive cost-per-student value and available year anchors, the script computes three piecewise-linear membership weights using the anchors for that year. The weights correspond to left-shoulder, triangular, and right-shoulder functions (Low, Medium, and High). The band label is the category with the maximum membership weight. Ties are resolved deterministically using the priority order Medium, then Low, then High (Figure 2).
The assigned label is recorded in the Band column, and a deterministic numeric mapping is recorded in Band_Score_0_to_1 (Low 0.0, Medium 0.5, High 1.0). The Fuzzy Bands sheet records the anchors used for each record alongside the membership weights and the assigned label. \EdefEscapeHexbm:results.1bm:results.1\EdefEscapeHex7 Results7 Results\hyper@anchorstartbm:results.1\hyper@anchorend
7 Results
Results are reported from the processed workbook and the execution logs produced by the pipeline. Numeric values in Sections 7.4–7.7 are synthetic examples used for illustration and are not attributable to any institution.
bm:results-1.2bm:results-1.2\EdefEscapeHex7.1 How to read the workbook7.1 How to read the workbook\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-1.2\hyper@anchorend
7.1 How to read the workbook
A practical reading order is Processing Summary, Trend Analysis, Report, then Fuzzy Bands. This sequence starts with provenance and counters, moves to school-by-year values, then to subject-level components, and ends with the categorical summary.
-
1.
Processing Summary. The Processing Summary sheet records a SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes to identify the input snapshot used for that run. It also lists row-handling and grouping counters, including boundary cases such as missing values treated as zero for aggregation and undefined ratios where cost 0 and student count 0.
-
2.
Trend Analysis. The Trend Analysis sheet provides a school-by-year table of derived cost-per-student values. Its colour scale is anchored within each year, supporting choropleth-style comparison across schools within each year. The banding is intended for within-year interpretation, with anchors computed independently for each year [3].
-
3.
Report. The Report sheet provides subject-level rows with inclusive on-costs, student counts, and derived ratios. It supports recomputing school totals within the processed workbook by summation of the subject-level rows.
-
4.
Fuzzy Bands. The Fuzzy Bands sheet provides a reading aid alongside the numeric ratios. It records year-specific anchors, membership weights on a 0 to 1 scale for Low, Medium, and High, and the resulting band label and Band_Score_0_to_1. Membership weights are graded labels rather than probabilities [17, 4, 11].
bm:results-2.2bm:results-2.2\EdefEscapeHex7.2 Produced sheets and their contents7.2 Produced sheets and their contents\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-2.2\hyper@anchorend
7.2 Produced sheets and their contents
The workflow writes a fixed-format processed workbook. In the default configuration, it contains four sheets:
-
•
Processing Summary records run metadata and counters. It includes InputfileSHA-256, Inputsheet, and Headerrow(1-based), along with row-drop and missing-value counters, group counts, and a per-year anchor summary.
-
•
Trend Analysis presents a school-by-year table of cost-per-student. It includes a textual “Methodology & Insights” block listing the year-specific anchors used for conditional formatting.
-
•
Report provides per-subject rows with per-year columns of the form YYYYInclOncosts, YYYYStudentCount, and YYYYInclOncostsPerStudent.
-
•
Fuzzy Bands provides a school-year table with CostperStudent, membership weights (Mu_Low, Mu_Medium, Mu_High), a band label (Band), a score (Band_Score_0_to_1), and anchors (Anchor_Min, Anchor_Median, Anchor_Max).
When invoked with --no-processing-summary, the Processing Summary sheet is omitted from the processed workbook.
bm:results-3.2bm:results-3.2\EdefEscapeHex7.3 Run metadata and counters7.3 Run metadata and counters\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-3.2\hyper@anchorend
7.3 Run metadata and counters
The Processing Summary sheet reports Input file SHA-256:
e68f42ddf3408e5c57d3b8385b699d78d3b2787f477ccbc541833b4f4aed4c21
The Processing Summary sheet reports:
-
•
Input identification: Inputsheet = data and Headerrow(1-based) = 1.
-
•
Rows seen and dropped: Rowsseen(includingdroppedrows), Rowsdropped(missingSchool/Subjectfields), Rowsdropped(yearnotdetected), and Rowsdropped(summaryrows:Total/Sum/Result).
-
•
Missing-value handling: Rowswithmissingcostvalues(treatedas0.0forsums), Rowswithmissingstudentcounts(treatedas0forsums), and Rowswithnegativestudentcounts(dropped).
-
•
Groups produced: Subject-Yeargroups and School-Yeargroups.
-
•
Boundary-case groups: Groupswithundefinedcost-per-student(cost>0andstudents=0) and Groupswithnoactivity(cost=0andstudents=0).
These counters record what was included, excluded, or treated as zero for aggregation, supporting interpretation of totals and ratios where missing values or boundary cases occur. They also support inspection by summarising how the run handled missing values, exclusions, and boundary cases. The counters are reported in the Processing Summary sheet. The processing log (cad_processor.log) records table detection and output write completion.
The execution log (cad_processor_execution.log) appends a tab-separated status record per run containing the input file name, output file name, and the input file SHA-256 hash.
bm:results-4.2bm:results-4.2\EdefEscapeHex7.4 Per-year totals from the Report sheet7.4 Per-year totals from the Report sheet\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-4.2\hyper@anchorend
7.4 Per-year totals from the Report sheet
In the synthetic example run, the per-year totals provide a compact check on how costs and counts roll up from subject-level rows.
Summing the per-year inclusive on-costs columns in the Report sheet yields normalised totals (2024 = 1.00) of 0.01 (2022), 1.06 (2023), 1.00 (2024), and 1.24 (2025). Summing the per-year student count columns yields normalised totals (2024 = 1.00) of 0.00 (2022), 1.04 (2023), 1.00 (2024), and 1.25 (2025). Each year’s total is divided by the 2024 total, so 2024 equals 1.00 and other years are expressed relative to that baseline (synthetic example outputs). These totals are consistent with Processing Summary, which notes that 2022 has no finite, positive cost-per-student values.
bm:results-5.2bm:results-5.2\EdefEscapeHex7.5 Anchors used for scaling and banding7.5 Anchors used for scaling and banding\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-5.2\hyper@anchorend
7.5 Anchors used for scaling and banding
The Processing Summary sheet lists anchors under Anchors used (finite positive School-Year values). For the logged run, 2022 is recorded as No finite, positive values, 2023 as min 9.0, median 14.0, max 28.0, 2024 as min 10.0, median 15.0, max 30.0, and 2025 as min 11.0, median 16.0, max 32.0. These are per-year anchors of the distribution of finite, positive school-year ratio values used for scaling and band assignment, and the values shown are synthetic examples. These anchors define the reference points for both colour scaling and fuzzy banding within each year. Anchors are computed independently for each year, so the banding is interpreted within each year rather than on a shared cross-year scale.
The Trend Analysis sheet applies a per-year colour scale using numeric anchors for the corresponding year column, and the scale is defined in the code as a three-point scale anchored at the year-specific minimum, median, and maximum values.
bm:results-6.2bm:results-6.2\EdefEscapeHex7.6 Fuzzy banding outputs and distribution7.6 Fuzzy banding outputs and distribution\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-6.2\hyper@anchorend
7.6 Fuzzy banding outputs and distribution
The Fuzzy Bands sheet contains school-year records for 2023, 2024, and 2025 and includes membership weights for Low, Medium, and High, with a band label that matches the maximum membership weight under deterministic tie-breaking (Medium, then Low, then High when membership weights are equal). The summary table in the Fuzzy Bands sheet reports per-year band counts. The reported counts are 2023 (Low = 1, Medium = 2, High = 2, Total = 5), 2024 (Low = 1, Medium = 2, High = 1, Total = 4), and 2025 (Low = 2, Medium = 2, High = 1, Total = 5). These counts provide a compact overview of how the eligible school-year records are distributed across the three bands within each year. Because the number of eligible records can differ by year, the counts summarise within-year distribution and are reported per year without implying cross-year change.
bm:results-7.2bm:results-7.2\EdefEscapeHex7.7 Worked example of membership computation7.7 Worked example of membership computation\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-7.2\hyper@anchorend
7.7 Worked example of membership computation
For a worked example, consider one school-year entry with cost-per-student value and anchors . In this workflow, are the year-specific anchor points used by the membership functions (minimum, median, and maximum anchors). The values are synthetic, rounded, and not attributable to any institution. Because , the Low and Medium degrees are computed using the linear segments between and in (1a) and (1b). The High degree follows from in (1c).
The Fuzzy Bands sheet records , , and for this record. The maximum membership is Low, so the band label is Low and the Band_Score_0_to_1 is 0.0. In practical terms, the record lies closer to the minimum anchor than to the median anchor for that year under the defined membership functions. The membership weights indicate the record’s placement relative to the year-specific anchors under the defined membership functions, and the label provides a concise category for reading the table. Membership weights are graded labels for within-year interpretation.
bm:results-8.2bm:results-8.2\EdefEscapeHex7.8 Pivot-table interpretation note7.8 Pivot-table interpretation note\hyper@anchorstartbm:results-8.2\hyper@anchorend
7.8 Pivot-table interpretation note
A pivot-table view constructed from the same input snapshot can provide an independent aggregation of costs and counts. When it applies equivalent grouping keys and row filters, the resulting totals align with the processed workbook tables produced by the script.
In practice, the check is most informative when the pivot-table mirrors the processor’s parsing rules, including treatment of missing values and the definition of cost-per-student (computed only when the aggregated student count is greater than zero). Discrepancies typically indicate differences in filtering, key normalisation, or boundary-case handling rather than arithmetic [10].
bm:discussion.1bm:discussion.1\EdefEscapeHex8 Discussion8 Discussion\hyper@anchorstartbm:discussion.1\hyper@anchorend
8 Discussion
The workbook artefacts produced by a run support direct checking of processing behaviour and derived tables. The Processing Summary sheet provides a compact run record. The Trend Analysis and Report sheets expose the aggregated values used for interpretation. The Fuzzy Bands sheet provides year-specific anchors and membership weights, allowing each categorical label to be verified against the numeric ratio.
bm:discussion-1.2bm:discussion-1.2\EdefEscapeHex8.1 Inspectability and boundary clarity8.1 Inspectability and boundary clarity\hyper@anchorstartbm:discussion-1.2\hyper@anchorend
8.1 Inspectability and boundary clarity
Inspectability in this workflow is supported by recomputation against a fixed snapshot and by artefacts that make row-handling decisions countable. The Processing Summary sheet records the detected input sheet and header row, the SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes, and counters for key row-handling outcomes produced during ingestion and aggregation [1, 13]. These counters allow reconciliation between what the run observed and what appears in the derived tables.
The workbook structure reinforces these checks. The school-year matrix in Trend Analysis provides an immediate view of cost-per-student patterns. The wide subject-level table in Report provides the corresponding values at a finer granularity. Together, these artefacts support inspection by relating reported cell values to the corresponding grouped totals and recorded counters.
bm:discussion-2.2bm:discussion-2.2\EdefEscapeHex8.2 Interpretability of fuzzy banding8.2 Interpretability of fuzzy banding\hyper@anchorstartbm:discussion-2.2\hyper@anchorend
8.2 Interpretability of fuzzy banding
The fuzzy banding layer is a compact, year-specific summary of each school’s relative position within that year’s school-year cost-per-student ratios. For each year, anchors are computed as the minimum, median, and maximum of the finite, positive ratios. Low membership follows a left-shoulder function anchored at the minimum and median, Medium membership follows a triangular function anchored at the minimum, median, and maximum, and High membership follows a right-shoulder function anchored at the median and maximum. The Fuzzy Bands sheet reports the anchors and membership weights alongside the ratio for each included school-year record.
Categorical labels are assigned deterministically. When membership weights are equal, ties are resolved in a fixed priority order: Medium, then Low, then High. Membership weights are presented as decision-support signals rather than probabilities, and the underlying ratios remain available for checking.
bm:discussion-3.2bm:discussion-3.2\EdefEscapeHex8.3 Boundaries and assumptions8.3 Boundaries and assumptions\hyper@anchorstartbm:discussion-3.2\hyper@anchorend
8.3 Boundaries and assumptions
-
•
Snapshot processing. The input workbook is treated as the reference snapshot for processing. The run record stores a SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes to support matching the snapshot used for recomputation [8].
-
•
Row-handling rules. Missing cost values and missing student counts contribute 0 (or 0.0, as applicable) to the relevant sums during aggregation, with occurrences recorded in run counters. Rows with negative student counts are excluded during ingestion, with occurrences recorded.
-
•
Ratios have named statuses. Cost-per-student is computed from aggregated totals. Groups with total student count greater than zero are labelled OK. Groups with both totals equal to zero are labelled No activity with a ratio of 0.0. Groups with non-zero total cost and zero total student count are labelled Undefined (0 students) with no numeric ratio.
-
•
Analytic scope. The analysis is descriptive rather than causal.
-
•
Fuzzy banding is year-specific. Anchors and membership weights are derived from finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratios for each year. The Fuzzy Bands sheet includes only the finite, positive cases and reports the anchors used for each year.
-
•
Pivot checks depend on equivalent rules. Spreadsheet pivot comparisons are most informative when they mirror the workflow’s grouping keys, filters, and row-handling rules.
bm:discussion-4.2bm:discussion-4.2\EdefEscapeHex8.4 Future evaluation steps8.4 Future evaluation steps\hyper@anchorstartbm:discussion-4.2\hyper@anchorend
8.4 Future evaluation steps
-
1.
Assess sensitivity of band assignments under alternative anchor definitions (for example, quartiles) computed from the same school-year cost-per-student ratios, while keeping membership function shapes fixed so that only the anchor choice varies.
-
2.
Record a separate presence indicator for each school-year combination, distinct from the numeric ratio, so that missing observations are distinguished from zeros in subsequent reporting and analysis.
-
3.
Add automated verification checks that re-aggregate from the recorded input snapshot and compare key totals and ratios to the generated workbook outputs under the same grouping and row-handling rules.
These steps extend the inspection-oriented design by strengthening verification and exploring the stability of the banding summary under controlled variations.
bm:conclusion.1bm:conclusion.1\EdefEscapeHex9 Conclusion9 Conclusion\hyper@anchorstartbm:conclusion.1\hyper@anchorend
9 Conclusion
A deterministic, rule-governed batch workflow is implemented to process Casual Academic Database (CAD) exports treated as spreadsheet snapshots. Given byte-identical input workbooks and a stable runtime environment, the workflow is intended to produce consistent outputs across reruns. The workflow transforms an input workbook into a processed workbook containing run metadata, trend tables, and a subject-level report, supporting checking by recomputation and comparison. The Processing Summary sheet records the SHA-256 hash of the input workbook bytes and the processing counters that describe observed row-handling outcomes.
Interpretability is supported by a lightweight fuzzy banding component that assigns Low, Medium, and High labels within each year using anchors defined as the minimum, median, and maximum of finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratios. The anchors, membership weights, and underlying ratios are reported together so that categorical labels remain traceable to the numeric values used to generate them.
RQ1 is addressed by specifying an evidence trail linking selected statements to concrete code elements and workbook locations, enabling behaviour to be checked against the produced artefacts. RQ2 is addressed by reporting year-specific anchors and membership weights alongside ratios, supporting within-year summaries while preserving the numeric basis for verification. Appendix A provides a claim-to-evidence matrix, Appendix B provides a reproducibility note, and Appendix C provides a short glossary.
bm:appendixA.1bm:appendixA.1\EdefEscapeHexAppendix A: Claim-to-evidence matrixAppendix A: Claim-to-evidence matrix\hyper@anchorstartbm:appendixA.1\hyper@anchorend
Appendix A: Claim-to-evidence matrix
Appendix A provides a claim-to-evidence matrix linking key statements to specific artefact pointers, including file names, function names, sheet names, and cell ranges where applicable. The matrix maps each claim to a concrete location in the artefacts. Tables 2–4 present the claim-to-evidence matrix, and Table LABEL:tab:citemap maps citations to claims.
bm:table5.2bm:table5.2\EdefEscapeHexTable 5. Citation map linking references to claims (A.4).Table 5. Citation map linking references to claims (A.4).\hyper@anchorstartbm:table5.2\hyper@anchorend
bm:appendixB.1bm:appendixB.1\EdefEscapeHexAppendix B: Reproducibility noteAppendix B: Reproducibility note\hyper@anchorstartbm:appendixB.1\hyper@anchorend
Appendix B: Reproducibility note
This note summarises the information needed to reproduce a run and verify that the outputs match a recorded input snapshot.
The processor reads an input workbook and produces a processed workbook and log files. Run metadata and counters are recorded primarily in the Processing Summary sheet, while the log files record run identifiers and table detection details:
-
•
CAD_Contract.xlsx (input workbook).
-
•
Processed_CAD_Contract.xlsx (processed workbook).
-
•
cad_processor_execution.log (execution log).
-
•
cad_processor.log (processing log).
The run logic in cad_processor.py is pinned to a specific repository commit to support inspection [5] and supports the following command-line flags:
-
•
--base-dir
-
•
--input-filename
-
•
--output-filename
-
•
--verbose
-
•
--no-processing-summary
The default input filename in the script is CAD_Contract.xlsx, and the default output filename is Processed_CAD_Contract.xlsx. Input and output names are resolved relative to inputs/ and outputs/ under --base-dir (or the project root when --base-dir is omitted).
The script computes a SHA-256 value over the input workbook bytes [8] and records that value in the logs and, when the Processing Summary sheet is included, in that sheet. The SHA-256 value serves as a content hash for the input snapshot. If any byte in the input workbook differs, the SHA-256 value is expected to differ, which supports traceability by allowing an analyst to check whether a processed workbook corresponds to the recorded input snapshot, without implying upstream correctness. If a processed workbook is edited after generation, the pipeline can be rerun from the recorded input snapshot and rule set and the regenerated workbook compared against the provided workbook to support inspection.
A minimal folder layout consistent with the artefacts is:
project_root/
src/
cad_processor.py
inputs/
CAD_Contract.xlsx (or another extract workbook)
outputs/
Processed_CAD_Contract.xlsx
An example invocation is:
python src/cad_processor.py
--input-filename CAD_Contract.xlsx
--output-filename Processed_CAD_Contract.xlsx
The output workbook contains the following sheets:
-
•
Processing Summary: run metadata, counters, and per-year anchors (omitted only when invoked with --no-processing-summary).
-
•
Trend Analysis: school-by-year cost-per-student matrix and the “Methodology & Insights” block.
-
•
Report: subject-level report with per-year totals, student counts, and per-student ratios.
-
•
Fuzzy Bands: per-school-year ratios with anchors, membership weights, and band labels.
bm:appendixC.1bm:appendixC.1\EdefEscapeHexAppendix C: Key termsAppendix C: Key terms\hyper@anchorstartbm:appendixC.1\hyper@anchorend
Appendix C: Key terms
This glossary defines key terms used in the paper.
- Aggregation
-
Aggregation combines row-level values into subject-year totals and school-year totals for inclusive on-costs and student counts.
- Anchors
-
Anchors are three reference values computed separately for each year from the set of finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratios across schools. They are recorded in the workbook and used to parameterise the membership functions. The anchors are the minimum, the median, and the maximum of the eligible ratios. The median is the middle value when the count is odd, and the average of the two middle values when the count is even.
- Boundary handling
-
Boundary handling is the rule-based treatment of missing values and zero-denominator cases during preprocessing and ratio computation. In this workflow, missing or non-numeric cost values are treated as 0.0 for aggregation and missing or non-numeric student counts are treated as 0, with counters incremented. The processed workbook records the ratio as undefined when the total cost is greater than 0 and the total student count is 0 (for example, inclusive on-costs of 50,000 with a student count of 0), and it records a ratio of 0.0 when both totals are 0 (No activity).
- Code version
-
Code version refers to the implementation used for a given run.
- Cost-per-student
-
Cost-per-student is inclusive on-costs divided by the student count when the student count is positive. When the student count is 0, the ratio is recorded as 0.0 when inclusive on-costs are also 0 (No activity). Otherwise, it is recorded as undefined. For example, inclusive on-costs of 50,000 with a student count of 10 yields 5,000.
- Deterministic
-
Deterministic means that, with byte-identical input workbook bytes and the same code version, rule set, and runtime environment, the processor should produce the same processed workbook. This includes the same counters, anchors, membership weights, and band labels. Inputs can change between runs (for example, monthly extracts that add new rows), which changes the resulting ratios, anchors, and labels. If the rule set changes, subsequent runs apply the updated rules, and that change is reflected in the code version and the resulting artefacts.
- Deterministic tie-breaking
-
Deterministic tie-breaking yields a single band label when two membership weights are equal [11]. For example, with anchors min , median , and max , a ratio of yields and . Without a tie rule, this boundary value could be described as either Low or Medium. In this implementation, ties are resolved by a fixed priority order: Medium, then Low, then High, so the label is Medium. Similarly, a ratio of yields and , and the assigned label is Medium.
This is a design choice that favours the central band at boundaries, so a boundary point is not pushed to an extreme label. In these examples, at the boundary points ( and ), the membership weights are equal for two adjacent bands. This is the sense in which the evidence is symmetric, and deterministic tie-breaking selects the central label rather than pushing the boundary point to an extreme. If a degenerate anchor configuration produces a tie that does not involve Medium, the same fixed order still resolves the tie deterministically, with Low preferred over High.
- Extracted workbook
-
An extracted workbook is the input workbook used by the workflow.
- File-based extract
-
File-based extract means the workflow reads an extracted workbook file.
- Input hash
-
A SHA-256 hash is computed from the input workbook bytes and recorded in the processed workbook and logs. It links each output to the specific input snapshot used for that run.
- Fuzzy banding
-
Fuzzy banding maps each finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratio (in years with defined anchors) to three membership weights for the bands Low, Medium, and High [17, 11]. The membership weights are computed from year-specific anchors (minimum, median, maximum) using simple piecewise-linear membership functions. A single band label is then assigned by selecting the highest membership weight and applying deterministic tie-breaking when degrees are equal (priority order: Medium, then Low, then High) [11]. For example, with anchors min , median , and max for that year, a ratio of yields , , and . Because Low and Medium are tied, deterministic tie-breaking assigns the band label Medium.
- Fuzzy Bands
-
Fuzzy Bands is the output sheet that records per School-Year Cost per Student, membership weights (Mu_Low, Mu_Medium, Mu_High), the selected Band and Band_Score_0_to_1, and the anchors (Anchor_Min, Anchor_Median, Anchor_Max).
- Hash function
-
A hash function maps input bytes to a fixed-length value. In this workflow, the saved input workbook file is read as bytes and the SHA-256 value is computed over those bytes. The value is recorded in the processed workbook as a hash of the input snapshot used for that run.
Figure 3 shows the helper that reads the saved input workbook file as bytes (in fixed-size chunks), updates the SHA-256 digest, and returns the hexadecimal digest string.
- Inclusive on-costs
-
Inclusive on-costs are the cost totals used in the cost-per-student ratio for casual academics in the CAD extract. “Inclusive” refers to base casual academic cost plus on-costs (for example, if a base cost is 40,000 and on-costs are 10,000, then inclusive on-costs are 50,000). The CAD extract representation used here excludes inclusive on-costs for continuing staff.
- Inspection trail
-
Inspection trail refers to recorded run metadata, counters, and intermediate values that allow inputs, processing, and outputs to be traced in the workbook. Examples include the input file SHA-256 value, the detected input sheet and header row, rows seen, rows dropped for missing keys, rows dropped where year is not detected, rows dropped for summary rows, and per-year anchors used for fuzzy banding.
- Membership weights
-
Membership weights are values in that represent partial membership of a ratio to each fuzzy band [17, 4, 11]. They are treated as graded labels rather than probabilities [17, 4, 11]. For example, with a ratio of and anchors min , median , max , the workflow yields , , and , which indicates that the value sits exactly on the boundary between Medium and High under the defined anchors. In this implementation, the deterministic tie-breaking rule selects Medium at such boundaries (priority order: Medium, then Low, then High), so the reported band label is Medium [11].
- Membership functions
-
Membership functions map a ratio to membership weights using the year-specific anchors [11]. With anchors min , median , and max , the workflow uses a linear decrease for Low from the minimum anchor to the median, a peak for Medium at the median, and a linear increase for High from the median to the maximum anchor [11]. The resulting membership weights and assigned labels at five reference ratios are:
-
•
: , , , label Low.
-
•
: , , , tie, label Medium.
-
•
: , , , label Medium.
-
•
: , , , tie, label Medium.
-
•
: , , , label High.
At boundary points, weights are equal for adjacent bands, and deterministic tie-breaking selects the central label.
-
•
- On-costs
-
On-costs are employer costs in addition to base salary or wages. In an Australian context, examples include superannuation, payroll tax, workers’ compensation, and leave entitlements. On-costs are included in the inclusive on-costs values for casual academics reported in the extracted workbook.
- Processed workbook
-
A processed workbook is the fixed multi-sheet workbook produced by the workflow.
- Processing Summary
-
Processing Summary is the output sheet that records Input file SHA-256, detected table identifiers (Input sheet and Header row (1-based)), and row- and group-level counters.
- Report
-
Report is the output sheet that lists subject-level rows (keyed by School, Subject No., and Subject) with per-year columns of the form YYYY Incl Oncosts, YYYY Student Count, and YYYY Incl Oncosts Per Student.
- Row-handling counters
-
Row-handling counters record how rows are included, excluded, and treated during preprocessing, and provide a compact summary of row-level data-quality conditions [10]. They include counts of rows dropped due to missing School, Subject No., or Subject identifiers, rows dropped because a year cannot be detected, and rows dropped because the export contains summary rows (for example Total, Sum, or Result). They also include counts of rows where cost or student count is missing and therefore treated as for aggregation, and rows where the student count is negative and therefore dropped.
For example, in a run with rows seen in the export snapshot, the counters might record:
-
•
summary rows dropped (for example, rows labelled Total),
-
•
rows dropped due to missing School, Subject No., or Subject fields,
-
•
rows dropped because a year could not be detected from the Teaching Session field,
-
•
rows with missing cost values treated as for sums,
-
•
rows with missing student counts treated as for sums,
-
•
row with a negative student count dropped.
-
•
- Rule set
-
Rule set is the fixed set of transformation rules applied in the workflow.
- Rule-governed
-
Rule-governed means the workflow applies fixed transformation rules rather than training or optimising a model.
- Run metadata
-
Run metadata records values detected from the input snapshot and counts produced during processing so that a run can be inspected and compared with later reruns [12, 7, 1, 13]. In this workflow, run metadata includes the detected input sheet name and header row, the input file SHA-256 hash, row-handling counters, and the year-specific anchors used for fuzzy banding.
For example, a Processing Summary may record:
-
•
Input sheet: CAD Export,
-
•
Header row (1-based): ,
-
•
Input file SHA-256: d4c3… (abbreviated example, 64 hex characters in full),
-
•
Rows seen (including dropped rows): ,
-
•
Rows dropped (summary rows: Total/Sum/Result): ,
-
•
Rows dropped (missing School/Subject fields): ,
-
•
Rows dropped (year not detected): ,
-
•
Anchors used (finite positive School-Year values): : min , median , max .
These values are recorded to support practical inspection by recomputation and comparison, rather than to certify upstream correctness or completeness [7].
-
•
- SHA-256
-
SHA-256 is a standard cryptographic hash function that produces a fixed-length digest from input bytes. In this workflow, the script computes a SHA-256 hash from the saved input workbook bytes, so the resulting hash reflects the exact input file as stored (including workbook format and contents). The workflow records this hash to tie the processed workbook to the input snapshot used for that run.
- Stream-based approach
-
A stream-based approach refers to reading row data sequentially rather than loading the full worksheet into memory [15]. In this workflow, the script reads one row at a time from the input worksheet, updates running totals and counters, and then moves to the next row. The approach can reduce peak memory compared with loading all rows at once, because the script keeps only the current row and aggregated group state in memory [15].
- Student count
-
The student count is the denominator used in the cost-per-student ratio.
- Tie-breaking
-
Tie-breaking is the rule used to assign a single band label when two or more membership weights are equal [11]. In this implementation, a deterministic tie rule is applied so that the same ratio and the same anchors always yield the same band label. Ties are resolved by a fixed priority order: Medium, then Low, then High. For example, if and for a ratio, tie-breaking assigns the label Medium. If and , tie-breaking also assigns the label Medium. If Medium is not among the tied maxima, Low is selected over High.
- Trend Analysis
-
Trend Analysis is the output sheet that presents a school-by-year cost-per-student matrix and applies per-year conditional formatting anchored to that year’s minimum, median, and maximum values.
- Year-specific anchors
-
Year-specific anchors are anchors computed separately for each year. For a given year, the workflow takes the finite, positive school-year cost-per-student ratios across schools in that year and computes the minimum, the median, and the maximum [6]. These three values are recorded as anchors for that year and used to parameterise the membership functions applied to that year’s ratios.
For example, if the finite, positive ratios in a given year are , , , , and , then the anchors are min , median , and max . If a different year has ratios , , , , and , then the anchors for that year are min , median , and max .
- Zero vs missing vs undefined
-
Zero, missing, and undefined refer to distinct cases in how values are represented and how ratios are computed [10]. Zero means the underlying value is present and equals , for example total on-costs are with a positive student count, which yields a defined ratio of . Missing means a required value is absent in the extract row (blank or null) and is treated as for aggregation, with the occurrence counted in the row-handling counters. For example, if a row has cost blank and student count , the workflow counts a missing cost value and adds for that row’s cost contribution. Missing values contribute 0 to aggregation but remain distinguishable via the row-handling counters.
Undefined means the ratio cannot be computed because the denominator is after aggregation. For example, if a school-year group has total on-costs but total students , the ratio is undefined and the output records this as an Undefined (0 students) cost-per-student case. A related case is No activity, where both total on-costs and total students are , and the output records No activity.
